ORAL ANSWERS TO QUESTIONS

: . : MR.YASUSHI AKASHI, SPECIAL ENVOY OF JAPANESE GOVERNMENT : DISCUSSIONS

0217/09

1. . . ( .. ) (The Hon. M. M. Pemasiri Manage) - (2) :

() 2009 ?

asked the Minister of Foreign Affairs: SP (a) Will he inform this House whether Mr. Yasushi Akashi, the Special Envoy of the Japanese Government, came to Sri Lanka during the month of January in the year 2009?

(b) Will he state- (i) whether Mr. Yasushi Akashi came to Sri Lanka on an invitation of the Government of Sri Lanka; (ii) if so, who invited him to Sri Lanka as mentioned above; and (iii) the matters discussed by him with the above-mentioned parties? (c) If not, why?

[ ]

2009 08 1441 1442

( )

( - ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama - Minister of Foreign Affairs) , . . . 19 , , . . , , . . . ( .. ) (The Hon. M. M. Pemasiri Manage) .

( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama) 2002 . , . . . ( .. ) (The Hon. M. M. Pemasiri Manage) 2009 . ( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama) , .

. . ( .. ) (The Hon. M. M. Pemasiri Manage) . . ( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama) , .

. . ( .. ) (The Hon. M. M. Pemasiri Manage) . 2009 . ( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama) .

. . ( .. ) (The Hon. M. M. Pemasiri Manage) . ( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama) . . . ( .. ) (The Hon. M. M. Pemasiri Manage) ? , 2009 , . ( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama) . . . ( .. ) (The Hon. M. M. Pemasiri Manage) . [ ] ( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama) . - . . ( .. ) (The Hon. M. M. Pemasiri Manage) . ( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama) . . [ ] . Sir, Mr. Yasushi Akashi is the Special Representative -[Interruption.] Let me answer your Question. Sir, b (i) of the Question is very clear. What does it ask? It asks whether we have extended an invitation to the Special Representative to visit Sri Lanka. Mr. Yasushi Akashi, the Representative of the Government of Japan for Peace Building, Rehabilitation and Reconstruction in Sri Lanka was appointed in October 2002, during the UNP administration in Sri Lanka. Now that the JVP is part of the UNP, they can easily find answers within their own quarters. . [ ] . Thank you. ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) . . rose.

1443 1444

( ) (Mr. Speaker) .

( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake)

The Hon. Foreign Minister forgets that he was also a part of the then UNP Government when Mr. Yasushi Akashi was appointed. It was - [Interruption.] The Hon (Dr.) Rajitha Senaratne says - [Interruption.] Is that right? So, Hon. Minister, it was a situation where the Co-Chairs were appointed. The Question that has been asked by the Hon. Member of Parliament is a very straightforward one. He has come to Sri Lanka 23 times. During the UNP regime, he came only four times. How has he come on the other 19 times? If he was appointed by the UNP, then, why did you not stop him coming thereafter? It is very easy to put everything on the UNP. The good things of the UNP are what your Government is holding at the moment. He has come to Sri Lanka 23 times and how has he come on the balance 19 times, is what the Hon. Member is asking.

( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama) He wants to know whether Mr. Akashi has come on the invitation of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the answer is, "No." He is coming here being the Special Representative to Sri Lanka appointed during the UNP regime. ( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) So, why did you not stop it?

( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama) What is there to stop?

( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake) If he is a special invitee of the Government, you can stop him coming, because you are paying all his expenses.

( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama) There is no issue. I repeat, there is no issue. I would like to know the position of the JVP now in terms of - [Interruption.]

( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake)

Do not get caught in saying untruths. If he is a special invitee, the Government pays all his expenses. If he is not an invitee, then why does the Government pay all his bills?

( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama) Why should we? It is an appointment granted by the Government of Japan. Thank you.

( ) (The Hon. Ravi Karunanayake)

When he comes to Sri Lanka, the expenses are borne by the Government of Sri Lanka. Please do not say untruths in this House.

( ) (Mr. Speaker) .

( ) (The Hon. Anura Dissanayake) , . () (ii) , '' , '' . , . . . . . - [ ] . . [ ] . [ ] , . . . . . , - [ ] - [ ] . . . , . '' '' . . . ? ? ? ? , ? , .

asked the Minister of Local Government and Provincial Councils: (a) Will he inform this House - (i) the types of roads in the Pallepola Pradeshiya Sabha area;

(ii) the name and the length of each road; (iii) the length of each of the aforesaid roads that had been tarred or laid with concrete at the time this Pradeshiya Sabha was elected in the year 2006; (iv) the names of the roads that have been repaired by laying concrete up to December, 2008, after this Pradeshiya Sabha was elected in the year 2006; (v) the length of each road; (vi) the amount of money spent on it; and

(vii) the expenditure head from which this money was spent? (b) If not, why?

35 : 35 : LAND NO.35 IN THAWALAMA DIVISIONAL SECRETARY'S DIVISION : UNAUTHORIZED SETTLERS

0513/'09 5. ( ) (The Hon. Thilakaratne Withanachchi) , , , - (2) :

() (i) / 35 ;

? () ? () , ? () , ?

asked the Prime Minister, Minister of Internal Administration and Deputy Minister of Defence, Public Security, Law and Order: (a) Will he inform this House - (i) the number of unauthorized settlers in land No. 35 in Thawalama Divisional Secretary's Division in the Galle District , which belongs to the Land Reform Commission;

(ii) the names and addresses of those settlers; and (iii) how long they have been residing on this land? (b) Is he aware that road facilities and electricity supply have been provided to this village? (c) Will he state the time frame within which action will be taken to grant title deeds for these lands as these settlers have been living there for a long time, having built their houses and engaging in farming activities? (d) If not, why?

: : RATGAMA PRADESHIYA SABHA AREA : TELEPHONE COMMUNICATION TOWERS

asked the Minister of Local Government and Provincial Councils: (a) Will he inform this House - (i) the number of telephone communication towers installed by telephone companies in the Ratgama Pradeshiya Sabha area and the addresses of their locations; and

(ii) the relevant companies and the year? ( ) (The Hon. Janaka Bandara Tennakoon) , . ?

( ) (Mr. Speaker) .

( ) (The Hon. Janaka Bandara Tennakoon) * .

* : : Answer tabled: () , (i) 07 . 1. , . 2. , , . 3. , . 4. , , . 5. , . 6. , . 7. , , . (ii) 1. 2004 2. 2006 3. 2006 4. 2008 5. 2008 6 2008 7. 2009 () , (i) . (ii) , () , () (i) . (ii) . 6,56,100.00 . 6,56,100.00 (iii) (iv) . () .

0550/09 07 . . , . 1. 2004 , . 200/- 2. 2006 , . 200/- 3. 2006 . 200/- 4. 2008 , . 172,500/- 5. 2008 , . 172,500/- 6. 2008 , . 172,500/- 7. 2009 , . 172,500/- 1. Sharing of Antenna Structures 1.1 Antenna structures should be used on sharing basis for which the tariff schedule will be determined by TRCSL in consultation with the TIPSs. The minimum number of antenna structures that conform to the technical requirements will be approved for an identified Antenna Structure Farm. 1.2 The TRCSL will initiate the information of a new Antenna Structure Farm when the necessity arises. TISPs may propose such locations to TRCSL.

1467 1468

1.3 The antenna structure shall be designed and constructed to accommodate a minimum of 20 square meters of additional design antenna area (from the top portion for at least two other TSPs. Physical space required for fixing of the additional antenna shall be reserved at top portion. This allocation of additional design antenna area will be encouraged through incentive schemes. 1.4 Initially up to three requests will be considered to construct separate antenna structures within the Antenna Structure Farm. Subsequent applicants should share one of the available antenna structures. Applications for additional antenna structures will be considered only under special circumstances and such applications will be referred to the TAC with justification for such request. 1.5 The Antenna Structure Farm will be confined to a minimum feasible area by the TRCSL, subject to a maximum radius of 250m. 1.6 The distance between Antenna Structure Farms will be kept at a minimum separation of 4 km. 1.7 Both TSPs and TISPs may obtain approval to erect roof top masts of height not exceeding 20 meters from the roof top within or in between Antenna Structure Farms. 1.8 Broadcasting antenna structures are exempted from the clauses 1.3 and 1.4 provided that application is initially forwarded for an Antenna Structure to be used only for broadcasting purposes. 1.9 Cumulative radio frequency power density due to Antenna Structure Farm should be within the limits defined by ICNIRP and adopted by TRCSL provided that the maximum RF power levels allowed are as per Annexure I. 2. Height Clearance 2.1 Maximum height of the antenna structure shall be based on the recommendations of the CAASL, MOD and UDA. 3. Lightning Protection 3.1 The Antenna Structure premises should be provided with a comprehensive lightning protection scheme to minimize the lightning related damage and injury as per the Annexure II (a). 3.2 The antenna structure should conform to the guidelines specified in Annexure II (b) with regard to the lightning protection concerns. 3.3 Installation of the lightning protection system should be carried out by the TISP as per Annexure II (b). 3.4 An insurance cover shall be in place against any lightning related damage to the neighbourhood due to the existence of the antenna structure. 3.5 A report on the lighting protection system, and other specified information as per Annexure III, shall be submitted to TRCSL by TISP twice a year. 4. Electromagnetic Interference and Health Concerns 4.1 Base Station equipment shall comply with the EMC standards acceptable to TRCSL. 4.2 TRCSL will enforce and monitor maximum RF power density criteria defined by ICNIRP and adopted by TRCSL as per Annexure I. 4.3 Verification of compliance with stipulated standards will be carried out by TRCSL or a recognized institution to ensure public safety.

5. Environmental Concerns 5.1 Natural environment of the area shall be protected from any potential adverse impacts in accordance with CEA or PEA approval. 6. Construction of Antenna Structures 6.1 The Antenna structure and other related infrastructure should be designed and constructed in conformity with BS 8100. TIA/EIA 222F (or latest) or other equivalent international standard accepted by TRCSL. 6.2 All antenna structures with height exceeding 30m should be designed and detailed as post-disaster type structures. 6.3 All the structural designs, construction drawings and proposals are required to be certified by a chartered civil engineer who is specialized in structural design. 6.4 Institutes and individuals who do the certification should be registered with TRC. 6.5 Minimum of third-party insurance coverage of the risk of physical damage and injury should be taken during the construction of antenna structure. A copy of the same should be submitted to TRCSL before commencement of the development. 6.6 During the construction, the antenna structure should be installed with an aircraft warning light, as per CAASL recommendations. 6.7 TISPs should obtain development permits from respective Local Authorities. All the approving agencies are encouraged to establish electronic document transfer in order to expedite the approval process. 6.8 TISP who has received approval is required to complete the construction of the new antenna structure within six months from the date of granting the approval. Failure to meet this requirement without a valid reason acceptable to TRCSL will result in cancellation of the approval. The new antenna structure should be available for sharing within 03 months from the date of completion. 6.9 No Telecommunication Antenna Structure should be constructed without written approval of TRCSL. 7. Installation of Antenna Structures on Buildings 7.1 The structural stability of the buildings, which are primarily designed for purposes other than facilitating antenna structures, should be certified by a chartered civil engineer who is specialized in structural design, prior to the approval for the construction of the Antenna Structure. 7.2 The TISP should obtain the planning clearance from UDA within the areas declared under UDA Law. 7.3 Antenna structure outside the areas declared under UDA Law will be considered for approval with the consent of relevant Local Authorities. 7.4 Antenna structures less than 5m in height above roof top level are required to obtain clearance only from the MOD and CAASL. 7.5 A lightning protection system should be installed as per the Annexure II (b), to ensure the safety of occupants. 7.6 All antenna structures on buildings with total height exceeding 30m above ground level should be designed and detailed as post-disaster type structures. All proposals shall be certified by a chartered civil engineer who is specialized in structural design. 7.7 Installations of Antenna Structures on buildings should conform to all other Guidelines in this document.

2009 08 1469 1470

8. Maintenance of Antenna Structures 8.1 Lighting and painting of Antenna Structures must be in accordance with the specifications of CAASL. 8.2 Antenna structure operator should submit a monthly report in electronic form to TRCSL indicating the information as per format No: TRC/NW/MR - 01. 8.3 Maintenance of antenna structure shall be carried out in accordance with Annexure IV 8.4 Maintenance of Lightning protection system should be done by the TISP in compliance with specifications given in Annexure II (c). 9. Alteration to Antenna Structures 9.1 Upon justifiable request(s) made by concerned parties, the TRCSL, in consultation with relevant authorities, may consider removal or alteration to the structure or suspension of operation. In such case all costs should be borne by the TISP. 9.2 To ensure the safety of the public and property, an Antenna Structure should not be abandoned even for short periods of time, unless otherwise it is completely removed. The TISP should inform the TRCSL and make arrangements to either remove a non-operational installation or transfer it to another antenna structure operator. Until the antenna structure is removed or transferred and the TRCSL is informed the same, the TISP is responsible for the maintenance of the antenna structure in conformity with provisions specified. 9.3 Any structural alterations to the Antenna Structure of its supporting structure, beyond what has been envisaged in the approved design, require the certification of a chartered civil engineer who is specialized in structural design to get the approval of the TRCSL. 9.4 Removal of an Antenna Structure also requires insurance to be taken for the coverage of the risk of physical damage and injury during the removal of antenna structure. 10. Approval Procedure 10.1 TISP should submit an application as per Annexure V in the form of soft and hard copies. 10.2 Approval Procedure is as specified in Annexure VI 11. General 11.1 All relevant authorities such as CEA, PEA, UDA, CAASL, LA, CEB and TRCSL are required to facilitate, the TISPs in establishing antenna structures to provide telecommunication services on a priority basis, as telecommunication networks are a vital component of infrastructure development while addressing the public health & safety, economic, environmental and other impacts. 11.2 Appeals for any deviation from these guidelines caused by technical or commercial issues will be referred to the TAC who will meet once in a month.

4 PL 004619 (2009/12)

2009 08 1489 1490

President, College of Anesthetisiologists No. 6, Wijerama House Wijerama Mawatha Colombo 07.

Dear Sir,

CHANGE OF PRESCRIBING PATTERN OF PETHIDINE INJECTION

Further to my letter of 11.02.2008 on the above matter.

This is to bring to your king notice that there is no noticeable improvement to the situation described in our earlier letter (A copy of the letter is attached.)

Your would appreciate that this situation eventually leads to disposal of considerable quantities of narcotic which give rise to sever financial and legal complications.

Therefore we earnestly request to take up the matter with the parties concerned and take immediate action to avert further worsening of the situation.

Your fullest corporation in this regard would be greatly appreciated.

Thanking you

Yours faithfully

Dr. B. V. S. H. Beneragama

Director

Medical Supplies Division

Copies: 1. Secretaty Ministery of Healthcare and Nutritionfor information please

2, Director General of Health Servicefor information please

Note D/MSD

President, College of Anesthetists, No. 06, Wijerama House, Wijerama Mawatha, Colombo 07.

Dear Sir, CHANGE OF PRESECRIBING PATTERN OF PETHIDINE INJECTION It has been noted that the consumption rate of Pethidine injection is far below the forecast and hence a considerable stock of Pethidine injection is stagnated in our stores. Being a narcotic drug it comes under the control of International Narcotic Control Board, who determines and controls the annual allocation of narcotic quota. As such any considerable difference in the amount allocated and amount used would result in severe legal and financial complications. This matter was brought to the notice of the head of the institutions in our letter MSD/SCU/P-10/07 dated 23.07.2007 and requested them to collect their requirement in time but the response was hardly sufficient to address the problem. The table given below shows the summary of estimates and actual usage. ITEM 2005 2006 2007 2008 Estimate Issue Estimate Issue Estimate Issue Estimate Pethidine 195,008 125,231 175,208 128,766 208,887 135,296 108,590 Injection 50mg in 0.5ml Pethidine 287,614 236,437 333,545 208,970 362,541 171,979 204,887 Injection 75mg in 0.5ml One of the reasons that could have been attributed to this slow moving is the use of Fentanyl and Tramadol as substitutes for Pethidine resulting the consumption of Pethidine lower than the estimate and giving rise to a sharp increase of usage of Fentaryl and Tramadol. You would appreciate that prescribing substitutes for narcotic druges should not be done purely on therapeutic point of view but due considerations must be given to the facts such as lead time of procuring, the quantities of the orders being processed, the stock available in hand, international pharmaceutical regulation etc. Therefore you are kindly requested to educate your members on this issue and re-consider prescribing substitutes for Pethidine. Your fullest corporation in this regard would be greatly appreciated. Thanking you Yours faithfully Dr. B. V. S. H. Beneragama Director Medical Supplies Division

asked the Minister of Labour Relations and Manpower:

(a) Will he inform this House whether the Cabinet Memorandum No. 06/1540/230/039 dated 18.08.2006 has been submitted to the Cabinet by the then Minister of Labour Relations and Foreign Employment with regard to the payment of salary arrears of textile workers who were involved in the July strike of 1980?

(b) Is he aware that the Cabinet of Ministers approved the said Memorandum on the observation of the Minister of Finance and Planning and instructed the Ministry of Labour Relations and Manpower (formerly, Labour Relations and Foreign Employment) to make the relevant payments?

(c) Will he admit that affidavits indicating salary arrears have been issued accordingly in order to make payments after identifying the correct owners by the Commissioner General of Labour to make the payments in early December 2006?

(d) Will he submit to this House-

(i) the number of affidavits for which payments are to be made; and

(ii) their names and addresses?

(e) Will he state-

(i) whether necessary steps will be taken to pay the salary arrears of the relevant textile employees on the basis of above factors; and

(ii) if so, when?

(f) If not, why?

asked the Minister of Agricultural Development and Agrarian Services: (a) Is he aware that a part of the fallow paddy field of Kapugama lying by the Matara-Kataragama main road in the Devinuwara Pradeshiya Sabha area has been filled and a hotel has been built on it?

BOX 1577, COLOMBO CDS/OCDS/SECRET/12 (01) Secretary Ministry of Defence 3 August 2009 CHANGE OF ITEMS IN THE NORINCO FRAMEWORK AGREEMENT IN RELATION TO THE SRI LANKA ARMY EXPANSION PLAN Reference: A. Framework Agreement signed between Ministry of Defence and NORINCO-China on 16 December 2008. B. Discussion between the Secretary - Defence and the Chief of Defence Staff on 29 July 2009. 1. On 16 December 2008, the Ministry of Defence entered into a Framework Agreement as in reference A totaling to US $ (C & F) 327, 729, 208.25 with the NORINCO - China in regards to procuring of security items for the items for the Sri Lanka Army which were then in priority to address the battlefield requirements. Up to now, out of the agreed quantities of security items, the NORINCO - China had delivered only the items worth of US $ (C &F) 105,336,573.12 as in annex A to the letter and a balance of US $ 222,392,635.10 is still remaining. 2. Nevertheless, due to the successes / changes in the combat zones and for evident reasons the list of requirements needs to be amended & include additional to address the present and future necessities in relation with the Sri Lanka Army Expansion / Modernization Plan.

[ ]

* . . Produced at end of speech.

2009 08 1549 1550

Hence, taking into consideration the time schedule, the availability of serviceable Artillery assets, the battle field / land transporatation constrains and mobility for Infantry, it is requested to initiate immediate action to amend the list of items in the NORINCO Framework Agreement as in Annex B for procurement on priority. 3. In addition, request note that the suggested Armoured Personnel Carriers are for additional 6 & Mechanized Infantry Battalions (present available assets sufficient only for 3 x Battalions ) and estimation was done giving emphasis to Infantry mobility and rapid deployment as prime factors. 4. Further, in view of the time schedule of redeployment and expansion / modernization of the Sri Lanka Army, it is recommended that the finalizing of the suggested amendments / additions to be carried out with immediate effect to facilitate the deliveries in a practical time frame/

5. Forward for your kind consideration and appropriate action please.

G. S. C. FONSEKA RWP RSP VSV USP reds psc General, Chief of Defence Staff.

Copy to MGO Branch Dte to Plans Minute No. : MOD/09/038/Army dated 11.06.2009 MINUTES OF THE MEETING OF THE STANDING CABINET APPOINTED PROCUREMENT COMMITTEE (SCAPC) - JUNE 11TH, 2009 AT 4.15 P.M. Members Mr. Lalith Weeratunga, Secretary to H. E. the President - Chairman Mr. Gotabaya Rajapaksa, RWP, RSP, psc - Member Secretary, Ministry of Defence, Public Secretary, Law and Order Mr. Sumith Abeysinghe, Secretary to the Treasury - Member Mr. S. Amarasekara, Secretary, Ministry, of Highways & Road Development - Member In attendance Maj. Gen JJPST Liyange, Master Genral Ordance/SL Army (Representing the Commander of the Sri Lanka Army) Brig. NUMMW Senanayaka, Director Plans/SL Army PURCHASE OF 30,000 NOS 122 MM MBRL ROCKETS FOR RM-70 GRAD OF THE SRI LANKA ARMY (Extension for the LC and last date of shipment) 1. The SCAPC which met on 11.06.2009 at the Office of the Secretary/Deference, Public Security, Law & Order considered the letter dated 20.05.2009 sent by the Commander of the Army with regard to the procurement of 30,000 Nos. 122 mm MBRL Rockets for the SL Army and the Technical Evaluation Committee (TEC) report dated 08.12.2008 annexed thereto. 2. The following we observed by the SCAPC- (a) Cabinet of Ministers vide Cabinet decision numbered CM/08/0985/305/042/TBR dated 12.06.2008 has granted approval to procure 30,000 Nos. 122 mm MBRL Rockets for Rm 70 GRAD of the SL Army from M/s Way Industries a. s., Slovakia through M/s Lanka Logistics & Technologies Ltd (M/s LL&TL) at a total C & F cost of USD 6,750,000 (USD 225.00 x 30,000 Nos.).

6 - PL 004619 - (2009/12)

1551 1552

(b) Subsequently, based on the request done by the bidder and the recommendations made by the SL Army, the SCAPC has granted approval to revise the total C&F cost to read as USD 9,690,000.00. The Cabinet of Ministers has also approved the same at the Cabinet meeting held on 21.01.2009. (c) The SL Army had originated the Letter of Credit (LC) on 30.12.2008 subjected to the following conditions. Last date of shipping - 30.01.2009 Expire date of LC - 30.04.2009 (d) In the meantime, due to the delay in granting Export License by the Slovak Government, the supplier has appealed fro an extension of the date of shipping to read as 31.05.2009 and the Commander of the Army has recommended the suppliers request. (e) Subsequently, the supplier M/s Way Industries has made a further request to extend the last date of shipment as 30.06.2009 and the expire date of the LC as 30.07.2009. The Commander of the Army by letter dated 20.05.2009 has recommended the supplier appeal.. (f) On a quarry made by the Secretary/Defence, the Commander of the Army by letters dated 06.05.2009 and 07.05.2009 has highlighted that the requirement in question is vital due to following factors. i. Stock in hand has gone down below the minimum stock level. ii. This procurement is a necessity to decide the combat level. iii. Future restrictions in obtaining Export License from the European countries are also to be considered in making a decision in this regard. iv. The supplier has already obtained to relevant Export License and ready for shipping. 3. The SCAPC discussed the matter deeply and observed that at present MBRL rockets are not required. Hence, it was decided to keep this requirement down. Lalith Weeratunga Gotabaya Rajapaksa RWP,RSP, psc Secretary to H. E. the President Secretary, Ministry of Defence, Chairman Public Security, Law & order Member S. Amarasekara Sumith Abeysinghe Secretary, Ministry of Highways & Secreraty to the Treasury Road Development Member Member MINUTES OF THE MEETING OF THE STANDING CABINET APPOINTED PROCUREMENT COMMITTEE (SCAPC) - DECEMBER, 10TH, 2008 AT 4.15 P.M. Members Mr. Lalith Weeratunga, Secretary to H. E. the President - Chairman Mr. Gotabaya Rajapaksa, RWP, RSP, psc - Member Secretary, Ministry of Defence, Public Security, Law and Order Mr. Sumith Abeysinghe, Secretary of the Treasury - Member Mr. S. Amarasekara, Secretary, Ministry of Highways & - Member Road Development PURCHASE OF 30,000 NOS 122 MM MBRL ROCKETS FOR RM - 70 GRAD OF THE SRI LANKA ARMY (Price Enhancement) 1. The SCAPC which met on 10.12.08 at the Office of the Secretary/Defence, Public Security, Law & Order considered the letter dated 09.12.2008 sent by the Commander of the Army with regard to the procurement of 30,000 Nos. 122mm MBRL Rockets for the SL Army and the Technical Evaluation Committee (TEC) report dated 08.12.2008 annexed thereto.

2. The following were observed by the SCAPC -

(a) Cabinet of Ministers vide Cabinet decision numbered CM/08/0985/305/042/TBR dated 12.06.2008 has granted approval to procure 30,000 Nos. 122mm MBRL Rockets for RM - 70 GRAD of the SL Army form M/s LL&TL) at a total C&F cost of USD 6,750,000.00

(b) The approved unit cost of a 122mm MBRL rocket is USD 225.00 on C&F basis. However, the supplier has now reported that they are unable to maintain the initial quoted price due to the circumstances and events that delayed in obtaining the Export permit. Accordingly, the revised unit cost now would be USD 230.00 on FOB basis or USD 323.00 on C&F basis.

(c) Further, the supplier highlights that the additional cost for transport and the depreciation of US Dollar against Slovak Koruna were badly affected to this price escalation.

(d) M/s LL&TL has reported that this price enhancement occurred due to volatility in the market arising from;

i. Wide publicity given by the media for the on going war in Sri Lanka against terrorists. ii. New demand for similar products from Georgia, Kenya and Sudan.

iii. Awareness by the supplier the purchase of 10,000 Nos. MBRLs from M/s STV, Czech Republic at a FOB cost of USD 270.00 and CIF cost of USD 347.60 per unit.

(e) Commander of the Army who awaits the goods urgently reports that the revised price is reasonable when compared with the prices of the other suppliers for the same producet. Further, he highlights that they have no alternative source to satisfy above requirement at present.

(f) The TEC which scrutinized the new price proposal has reported that quoted price is reasonable and economical at this hour of time.

(g) In view of the above facts, Commander of the Army strongly recommends to procure 30,000 Nos 122 mm MBRL rockets for RM - 70 GRAD of the SL Army from M/s Way Industries a. s., Slovakia at a revised unit cost of USD 230.00 on FOB basis or USD 323.00 on C&F basis.

3. Considering the requirement and the recommendations made by the Commander of the Army, the SCAPC recommends to the Cabinet of Ministers to procure 30,000 Nos 122 mm MBRL rockets for RM - 70 GRAD of the SL Army from M/s Way Industries a. s., Slovakia at a revised unit cost of USD 323.00 on C&F basis. Accordingly, total cost now should read as USD 9,690,000.00 on C&F basis.

Lalith Weeratunga Gotabaya Rajapaksa RWP,RSP, psc Secretary to H. E. the President Secretary, Ministry of Defence, Chairman Public Security, Law & Order Meber

S. Amarasekara Sumith Abeysinghe Secretary, Ministry of Highways & Secretary to the Treasury Road Development Member Member

1571 1572

. , , .

[. . 12.42] . ( . ) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan) Venerable Presiding Member, we are once again debating the extension of the state of Emergency. It appears to me that this Government will never be able to rule this country under the normal laws of this land and will always look up to the Emergency to be in a position to govern this country. I wish to say a few things in regard to certain matters of utmost importance to the Tamil people, particularly to the persons who have been displaced in the Vanni. It would appear from the information available, that maybe around 50 per cent of the people who were originally confined to camps have left the camps, but there are still around 45 per cent of them in the camps. In regard to persons who have been taken to other districts, for instance, the districts in the Eastern Province, our information is that once the people are taken to the Eastern Province, they are merely dumped there and thereafter nothing else is being done for them - they are not being looked after in any way. Resettlement and rehabilitation in regard to such persons is totally non-existent. It is not happening - nothing is happening. The impression is also sought to be made that when the people are sent out of the camps it is a great achievement and that everything is all right thereafter. I am sorry that we have had to point out several times in the past and we have to point out now that these persons, before they were displaced consequent to the war, led honourable lives. They were in a position to live happily and peacefully on their lands, in their houses; they generated their income; they looked after their families. Today, they have lost their houses; they have lost all that they owned in this country and they have been reduced to a state of penury, destitution. Therefore, merely releasing them from the camps is not sufficient. These people have got to be rehabilitated. Their houses have got to be constructed. In many instances, the houses have been damaged beyond repair. Their livelihood must be restored. They must be in a position to commence their occupation. They must be in a position to generate an income with which they can look after their families.

We have always been complaining that the Government has no comprehensive plan in regard to these matters. It has been our complaint that the Government has no road map; the Government has not made its positions clear. Why can the Government not be transparent and let everybody know what is happening; what their plans are; what they are going to do with these people; how they are going to be rehabilitated; what is going to be done for them in regard to housing; in regard to livelihood opportunities and so on and so forth? As a matter of fact, the international community, the foreign countries, are prepared to help substantially in the matter of rehabilitating these people. INGOs funded by foreign governments are prepared to help lavishly in regard to rehabilitating and resettling these people. But, we are inclined to the view that many of these countries are holding back the assistance that they can give, on account of the fact that the Government has no definite plan in regard to resettlement and the Governments lack of transparency in regard to this whole question is being looked at with misgiving by many persons who can play a very useful role in looking after these people who need much assistance. The second point I want to make, is that there were some High Security Zones in the Northern Province and the Eastern Province and these zones continue to be effective and are still being maintained as High Security Zones though the war has come to an end. It is our submission that there is no justification whatever for these High Security Zones to continue any longer. The rationale for these High Security Zones was that the LTTE had artillery fire and they fired with artillery at certain institutions like the Palaly Airport. To ensure that LTTE artillery fire would not reach these institutions as the airport a zone was declared as a High Security Zone. In other words, the purpose was to keep these institutions beyond the range of LTTE artillery fire. Today, the LTTE is not there; the artillery is not there; the artillery fire is not there. The Government is in effective control of all the territory in that area and I want to raise the question as to what justification there can be for the continuance of these High Security Zones, which, I think, is causing a great deal of inconvenience to the Tamil people. In Valikamam North in the Jaffna District, the people who were displaced as far back as 1989 and 1990 on account of the High Security Zone - for almost for the past 20 years, two long decades - have not been able to live on their lands. Twenty eight thousand families consisting of about 100,000 people were displaced from the High Security Zone. The vast majority of them, about 60 per cent, were people depending on agriculture on land in the High Security Zone. There were 45 Grama Sevaka Divisions covered by the High Security Zone, an entire territory of 59.5 square kilometres, about 60 square

[ . . . ]

2009 08 1573 1574

kilometres of territory, which originally had 28,000 families, about 100,000 people. All the houses have been destroyed and the people have been compelled to live as refugees in welfare centres or with their friends and relatives in other parts of the Jaffna District. The famous Naguleswaram Temple and the famous Maviddapuram Kandaswamy Temple are inside the High Security Zone. There are other temples and churches inside the High Security Zone. Now, the war is over, Venerable Presiding Member. Why should not these 100,000 people get back to their lands, to their houses? You must take them back to their lands and their houses. Their houses must be rebuilt. Their position is as bad as that of the IDPs. They must get back to their lands; their houses must be rebuilt; they must be helped to start life all over again and they must stat life. Similarly, in Trincomalee, in the Sampur-Koonitivu area, the Mutur-East area, 1,486 families have not yet been resettled. They have been kept out of that area and I have in fact furnished particulars in this House on a previous occasion on this issue. About 2,795 acres of private land belonging to these people, almost 3,000 acres of land, is caught up within this High Security Zone, to which the people cannot return. You are virtually confiscating their land. When the President addressed the SLFP Convention that year, on the 04th of September, 2006, he said, Our armed forces have captured Sumpur for the welfare and benefit of the people living there. If Sampur has been captured for the benefit and welfare of the people living there, surely people must be able to go back to their lands. That is not happening, I want to urge that the High Security Zones be dismantled without further delay. In fact, I urge that the High Security Zones be dismantled before the forthcoming Presidential Election. At least the process of dismantling must commence before the Presidential Election and it must be completed before the Parliamentary Election. You cannot be keeping tens of thousands of people out of their residences and their agricultural land when there is no justification whatever any longer for these lands to be regarded as High Security Zones, because the LTTE is not there; the artillery is not there; there is no firing there; the entire territory is under your control and how can you justify their being High Security Zones? I do not think this situation can be allowed to continue. Similarly, the Muslim IDPs from the North who have been living in Puttalam and other parts of the country must also be taken back and resettled. We are sorry to observe that the Government has no comprehensive plan in regard to the resettlement of the Muslim IDPs. We call upon the Government to effectively take action to resettle the Muslim IDPs in Jaffna before the Presidential Election and complete the resettlement before the Parliamentary Election is over.

These are challenges the Government must be prepared to face. I mean, things have been done in a way which seems to suggest that the Government has no serious commitment in regard to these matters. Things have been done in an ad hoc way - things have not been comprehensively planned and things have not been properly implemented - that is our complaint. So, Venerable Presiding Member, these are matters which we raise on the Floor of this House quite frequently, but nobody takes them too seriously.

But now with the elections in the offing, at least I hope that there will be a little more seriousness and that you will not fail in your duty to ensure that these people are not deprived any longer of their lands on which they would like to reside, on which they have lived for generations and centuries and on which they must carry on their cultivation and their occupation.

The next matter I want to raise is the question of demilitarization. We have urged several times - in fact, when we met the President on the 7th of September we urged with him - that demilitarization must commence, that military camps established in the Northern and Eastern Provinces after the commencement of the war must be dismantled and that we must go back to the situation prior to the commencement of the war.

( ) (The Presiding Member) .

. ( . ) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan)

No, Venerable Presiding Member, I have got time. I will take my Partys time. We have been urging that they must get back to the situation which prevailed prior to 1983 and there is no need for these camps now that the war has come to an end. The Tamil people must have the freedom to live with dignity as free citizens. The Sri Lankan State should not treat them like second-class citizens. But, what is happening today? I am told that along the A-9 road - one does not see this publicly when one travels on the A-9 road - a little distance inside, army camps are being established. It is also happening on the A-32 road between Poonarin and Mulangavil, some distance away from the road, army camps are being established. In a village called Kavtharimunai, a big army camp has been established recently. Why are you doing these things? Is this the reason why you are keeping INGOs out of these areas? Is this the reason why you do not want foreign governments to come and help the people living in those areas? Is it the position that you feel that if INGOs and foreign governments get involved in resettling people, in rehabilitating these people, these things will come to light? Large extents of land are being

1575 1576

taken for this purpose. So, far from demilitarizing the situation in the North-East, we are sorry to say, Venerable Presiding Member, that what is in fact happening is further militarization which is unacceptable and which I say, must stop. What is most alarming is, there is information that these camps are being constructed with Chinese assistance. We have reliable information that China is assisting the Government to construct these camps. They are prefabricated camps and the fear is that there can be not merely camps but cantonments, which would mean that in addition to the camps there would be settlement of army personnel and their families around these camps.

( ) (The Hon. Mano Ganesan)

That is exactly what China is doing in Tibet. . ( . ) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan)

The Chinese Government is engaged in assisting the Sri Lankan Government to construct these camps and these cantonments. This is totally an unacceptable situation and in my submission, cannot continue and such action should be stopped immediately. I mean, I do not understand the purpose of trying to saturate the North-East with army personnel even after you have won the war. I mean, you may fear that there may be some subversive activity, but, surely, that can be handled by brain rather than brawn, by better intelligence rather than saturating these areas with army personnel, thinking that you can thereby keep the Tamil civilians completely under your control. The simple question is this. Are you prepared even after the war is over to ensure that there is only civilian rule in the North-East, in which the Tamil-speaking people in the North-East - the Tamils and the Muslims - have an adequate role to play in such a civilian rule or, is it your position that even though the war is over, you want to have military rule in the North-East and keep the Tamil people in particular, completely under military control? This is a very crucial question that the Government must be prepared to answer. Are you prepared to concede that there must be, in the North-East, a civilian rule in which the Tamil-speaking people should have an adequate and effective role or, is it your position that even though you may have won the war, you want to keep the Tamil-speaking people, the Tamil people in particular, under your complete military control and continue to humiliate them, continue to harass them, continue to insult them? I do not think, Venerable Presiding Member, this situation can continue. Particularly with the information that is now available to us in regard to further militarization, construction of further camps and the involvement of the Chinese Government in assisting the Sri Lankan

Government to construct these camps, we are very concerned about what the true intentions are, what the real intentions are and where these will all lead to. And we say that even the Emergency Regulations are extended monthly on account of these activities that the Government is engaged in. The Government feels that it cannot sustain without Emergency Regulations being enforced when it is engaged in such questionable activities. That is my complaint. In fact, your inability to evolve an acceptable political solution, in my submission, is the main cause for all these things happening. An acceptable political solution, not even a proposal in regard to a solution, has been placed before the people of this country in the past four years though the Government has made several commitments in regard to this matter to the international community, India in particular - but nothing has been done. I might, Venerable Presiding Member, at this moment refer to a Suo Motu statement made by the Minister of External Affairs of India in the Rajya Sabha on recent developments in the North-East of Sri Lanka. He said, in the course of a long statement he made, I quote: Government is keen to see the revival of the political process in Sri Lanka, which will meet the legitimate interests and aspiration of all communities, including the Tamils and the Muslims, within the framework of a united Sri Lanka. Revival of such a political process and an inclusive dialogue would help bring the minority communities into the political mainstream. We have continued to emphasize to the Sri Lankan Government to put forward a meaningful devolution package . Not any package, "a meaningful devolution package". .that would go beyond the 13th Amendment." It must go far beyond the Thirteenth Amendment. I further quote: We will remain engaged with them through this process of transition and reform. That is the statement made by the Indian Minister of External Affairs in the Rajya Sabha when he spoke on the situation in the North-East. So, the Government is engaged in all these activities in the North-East, whether it is militarization, further militarization, not engaged in demilitarization, maintenance of High Security Zones, keeping out foreign governments and INGOs from the North-East when they can contribute very effectively and extensively to resettlement and rehabilitation in those areas. All this is happening because the Government is unable to come up with a political solution and the Government thinks that the military presence and militarization is inevitable in that situation.

Before I conclude, Venerable Presiding Member, I want to refer to a very serious act of vandalism that has occurred in the Trincomalee District very recently, in about the past two weeks. There was an ancient Sivan temple, Sir, said to have been established by the much venerated Hindu Munivar Agasthiar called the Agasthiar Sthapanam.

[ . ]

2009 08 1577 1578

It is believed to be over 2500 years old and situated in a village called Thangaveli, on the borders of the Mahaweli river. The temple has gone into ruins. It was in a jungle area. In fact, during the peace time, on the request of the people in that area, I and my Colleague, the Hon. Thurairetnasingam, went to this area and we laid a foundation stone to construct a new temple which could not be continued on account of the disturbed situation. Recently, in the course of the past two weeks, the Sivalingam has been broken; pillars have been damaged; statutes have been damaged and some people have been engaged in an utter vandalism in destroying the remnants of that old, historic temple believed to be over 2500 years old. This is what happens when you have militarization. When you have the military present all around, when you have as your Government Agent of Trincomalee an Army official, when you have as Governor in the North-East yet another armed services official, this is what happens. Now, I am told that the Government Agent has sent his Divisional Secretary to that area and they are trying to do some repairs. What repairs can you do, having demolished the Sivalingam, having demolished pillars, having demolished statutes - ancient, historic statutes?

( )

( - , ) (The Hon. Dew Gunasekara -Minister of Constitutional Affairs and National Integration)

When did this happen?

. ( . ) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan)

People go there off and on. There are chena cultivators, people go there to collect firewood, people go there to perform certain ceremonies and when they went on the 28th of November, they saw this for the first time. It must have happened a few days before that. So, this is what is happening in our areas. Can this happen in a Buddhist country? I am happy, Venerable Thero, that you are presiding. Is this an act that can happen in a Buddhist country where Buddhism is truly practised?

( ) (The Hon. Dew Gunasekara)

It has happened in other parts of the country as well.

. ( . ) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan)

I am not concerned about other parts of the country. Are you saying that because it happens in other parts of the country it must continue to happen ?

( ) (The Hon. Dew Gunasekara)

I am not justifying. . ( . ) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan)

Where does it happen now? In Christian churches, Hindu temples, maybe in mosques. It is a very serious matter. This is sacrilege, not merely vandalism but downright sacrilege - unpardonable. I met the President on last Wednesday and I brought this to his notice personally and told him that there has been such a serious incident which has taken place in Trincomalee. So, this is an effort on the part of people to further militarization, to Sinhalize the place, remove all evidence of ancient Hindu monuments in such a way that you can settle Sinhalese people, have the Army around and make this place a Sinhalese territory. I am not against the Sinhalese people. I have nothing against them. I have always treated them with a lot affection and respect, but we must protest Venerable Presiding Member, when these things happen. So, I want to impress upon the Government that they must dismantle these High Security Zones, they must stop further militarization, they must engage in demilitarization, they must stop these acts of vandalism, sacrilege by certain persons and there must be effective resettlement and rehabilitation that will enable the internally displaced Tamil persons to recommence life in an effective way and that the Muslim refugees, living in Puttalam and other parts of the country, must be resettled at the earliest in Jaffna. I thank you, Venerable Presiding Member.

( ) (The Presiding Member) , . , . 10 .

Sir, I rise to a point of Order.

( ) (The Deputy Speaker) , ?

( ) (The Hon. Lalith Dissanayake) . [ ] , - [ ] , . ( ) (The Deputy Speaker) ? ( ) (The Hon. Lalith Dissanayake) , . . . . . [ ] . . . [ ]

1615 1616

( ) (The Deputy Speaker) . [ ] [. . 3.02] ( ) ( - ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama - Minister of Foreign Affairs)

My good Friend, it is my turn now. -[Interruption.] ( ) (The Hon. Lalith Dissanayake) ? ? [ ]

( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama) , . [ ] I am speaking. . [ ]

( ) (The Deputy Speaker) . .

( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama)

Hon. Deputy Speaker, I want to make a serious contribution to this Debate. I think the House was full of what we term in simple jargon as "noise". Now, we will get into more serious matters with regard to todays Emergency Debate, which we all should be part of. Today, the entire Debate centered round one key element - democracy. I appreciate that. Why has the forthcoming Presidential Election of 2010 become so much of an issue? Today, under the leadership of President Mahinda Rajapaksa, we are for the first time witnessing a country free of terror and full of liberty. So much so, all the political forces, both on the Government side as well as on the Opposition, have the benefit of enjoying tranquility in terms of a settled environment, a normal environment - an environment in which political parties can actively participate in a very important election for our country. That election is second to none other election in this country. It is an important election for all our communities, for the entire nation. As the Foreign Minister, I must share with every one of you the importance the foreign community attaches to this Presidential Election that will be held for the first time in a free Sri Lanka.

At the outset, let me confer the dues on President Mahinda Rajapaksa for bringing about this environment . Hon. Deputy Speaker, all the speakers from the Opposition were trying to go into the lighter effects of an important subject. My Friend, the Hon. Dayasiri Jayasekara - I hope he will remain here - went on to speak more in terms of - [Interruption.] He has more work other than to respect the House, the Parliament, for which his people - the voters of the Kurunegala District - have elected him. - [Interruption.] I can understand. I will not stand in his way. Today, the work for him also is that of an agent, because the UNP, for the first time in the history of the UNP, has no candidate of their own contesting at the most important election in the country. Whatever the strength they command in the country, today, for the first time, they have conceded defeat even before entering the race. Then comes the JVP. There again, they have not won a Presidential Election. The statistics of the Provincial Council Elections of 2008-2009 clearly show where they stand in terms of the national electorate. So, there is no issue with regard to the JVP. They must get themselves attached to anyone who comes forward as a Presidential candidate and we wish them well. But, the issue here is, the UNP. The UNP has no candidate and today they have a joint candidate or whom we term as a candidate who has been proposed -

( ) (An Hon. Member)

A common candidate. ( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama)

What is that? Common? But, it cannot be a common candidate also. . Therefore, this joint candidate, General Fonseka, a retired General of the Army, is not the issue. For the first time in the history of Sri Lanka, one who has represented the very establishment that is protecting the territorial integrity and the sovereignty of a democratic nation and who was holding office both as the Army Commander and the Chief of Defence Staff, has within a period of two weeks, after ceasing to hold that office - that coveted office - has entered the political race, contesting or challenging the very establishment that he served. That is the most important aspect of this whole issue. He is challenging the very military establishment; he is challenging the Commander-in-Chief; he is challenging the President of Sri Lanka; he is challenging the Army in which he served as the Army Commander; he is challenging the other armed forces, of which he was the Chief of Defence Staff and he has now become a political candidate. But still, he does not seem to belong to a political party even to be called a political candidate. Whatever it maybe, the issue here is, to what extent have we undermined the

2009 08 1617 1618

establishment of Sri Lanka, the sovereignty of our country? A person holding the office of the Army Commander or the Chief of Defence Staff of any country cannot - it is never done as a matter of principle and to maintain the integrity of that office - deal with other countries either privately or officially, unless it is done through the channels that are meant for such communication and such conduct. That is what we term as the protector of the State. The President or the defence establishment cannot deal with foreign embassies or foreign missions in any direct manner whilst visiting them in their premises. We have not had such instances.

But now, we are aware of such situations that have developed and there is concern, a reasonable fear that we maintain, that the countrys territorial integrity and the sovereignty, to some extent have, have been undermined or have been exposed by some actions of this officer concerned. Where do you find an officer being permitted to be interrogated on foreign soil, an officer with whom privileged information is retained? If one has been conniving, it is a serious offence in terms of the countrys Constitution and the legal system. Here is an instance where General Fonseka had been subjected to that type of conduct and this also brings to light to what extent the General concerned has undermined the sovereignty and the territorial integrity of our country.

These are important facts. Today revelations were made by the Hon. John Senewiratne of visits to certain countries where he had become privileged to be accommodated by arms manufacturers. These are important issues that we are discussing today. Therefore, everything is not rosy. No one seems to be all that innocent as they appear to be. There is so much beneath all what has been happening, which will come to light in due course.

( ) (The Deputy Speaker)

Hon. Minister, your time is over.

( ) (The Hon. Rohitha Bogollagama)

Sir, give me only one more minute. Sir, I must also bring to your notice the concerns that have now been expressed in terms of our efforts. Today, we have made major improvement and progress in the settlement of the IDPs. The concerns that were expressed earlier have now subdued. They are much less because the international community has seen the positive action that is taking place in Sri Lanka with regard to the settlement of the IDPs . We have made vast progress and the tides that have been generated will only make it possible for the Tamil brotherhood to become part and parcel of normal life in the North.

Then, in terms of the GSP concession, all the pessimism - and also to some extent the sarcasm - that have been expressed will not live long. Sri Lanka is confident and will be looking forward for the continuation of our engagement with the European Union and we will see how best that measurement will come into effect in terms of our engagement and Sri Lanka will not be a denied State. Then, it is very important to highlight the outcome of the CHOGM held in Trinidad and Tobago in 2009. Sir, I must express here our gratitude to the British Prime Minister, the Australian Prime Minister and to all other Heads of State who participated at the Commonwealth Heads of Government Meeting, 2009. Sir, I will now quote from my opening comments at the press briefing on the concluded CHOGM. Sri Lanka being endorsed at the recent summit to host the 2013 CHOGM on a proposal made by British Prime Minister Gordon Brown, is an important milestone in the consistent engagement of our country with the work of the Commonwealth. Since Australia and Mauritius had also offered to be host the CHOGM, Prime Minister Gordon Brown articulated the position that all three countries are equally qualified for this purpose. It was decided by the Commonwealth Heads of Government that Australia hosts CHOGM 2011 followed by Sri Lanka in 2013 and Mauritius in 2015. This consensual endorsement of Sri Lanka by the entire membership of the Commonwealth singularly demonstrates the acceptance of Sri Lankas adherence to Commonwealth values and principles, with the country being a vibrant democracy. The credit goes to President Mahinda Rajapaksa for having raised Sri Lankas profile as the CHOGM will be held, for the first time in the independent history of Sri Lanka, in our country in 2013, which has been entirely endorsed by all the Heads of State of the Commonwealth countries, numbering 53. Thank you, Sir. [. . 3.14] . . ( . . ) (The Hon. K.V. Samantha Vidyaratne) , . , , . , , . . , . . , . . .

, . . , . , . . 10 . ! , . . . , . . . ( ) (The Deputy Speaker) . . . ( . . ) (The Hon. K.V. Samantha Vidyaratne) , . , , . , . . . . . . , 31 . , , , , , 26 . , . , . [ ] ( ) (The Deputy Speaker) . .

[. . 3.24] . . ( ) ( () . . - ) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala - Minister of Higher Education)

Mr. Deputy Speaker, the Emergency Debate is some kind of a Constitutional ritual enacted monthly inside this House for the purpose of discussing issues pertaining to the security of the State.

The major obstacle to development and security of the State was the separatist violence of the LTTE, which has now been destroyed by an effective political leadership provided by His Excellency the President. No armed force, whatever its experience and capacity, cannot achieve much without an effective and committed political leadership and this thesis was proved during the Second World War as well. Today, the conflict, which destabilized the country for more than 30 years, has come to an end and a new political situation has arisen as an aspect of the aftermath of the conflict which, in fact, was the sole cause for instability in this country. It was expected that the post-conflict political scenario after three decades of destruction and devastation of the national assets of this country would be used for the reconstruction of a great new society for Sri Lanka. What has happened now, Mr. Deputy Speaker? A new political scenario has emerged with the entry of Sarath Fonseka as the common candidate of the Opposition, which is in total disarray. Who was Sarath Fonseka a fortnight ago? That question has to be asked. All of us know who he was. He was wearing a military garb and claiming to function as the Chief of Defence Staff, which position he gave up a week back to become an ambitious politician. This is a man without an iota of political experience, without any experience in any civilian position, for that matter. He has become a politician overnight and he displays his ambitions for political power. Mr. Deputy Speaker, this portends a great danger for this country. I need to emphasize that. A military man, with 40 years of experience with the gun, is entering the political landscape of this country which, since 1931 experienced democratic government, and he wants to become the Presidential candidate at the forthcoming Presidential Poll. He is a person who carried the gun for a period of 40 years. This is a dangerous trend which needs to be arrested in this country. It portends a great danger for the very survival of democracy and it portends an equally powerful danger for the regional stability. India, as the most powerful neighbour of our country and as an emerging regional power, has to take note of this dangerous development in Sri Lanka. Therefore, a political analysis of this development needs to be done. The country expects it. Are we on the verge of a military dictatorship? That question has to be asked. Are we on the verge of a military dictatorship in this country with the assistance of both the UNP and the JVP? The JVP has been trained in the military tradition. Are we paving the way for an eventual military takeover in this country? Are we inviting the military to run the Sri Lankan State? Are we inviting the military through Fonseka to run the Sri Lankan State? These questions have to be asked in this House. One has to ponder on these major issues as the emerging scenario, as the emerging situation portends a great danger for the very survival of democracy in this country. The magnitude of it cannot be explained within a few minutes. It calls for an in-depth analysis as the

1623 1624

armed forces, due to our own follies, especially those of certain media institutions in this country, received unwanted recognition and publicity. They, through the post-conflict propaganda, entered the civilian political life of the nation. In my view, it was unnecessary and I always thought that the publicity they received was too much in the given context and in the given scenario. In the same way, Fonseka, a man imbibed with ambitions for power, made use of this scenario to make a debut at the next Presidential Poll. Since 1931 or for that matter, since 1948, Sri Lanka never faced a similar challenge. The entry of Fonseka into the political fray, in my view, is the most dangerous development in the history of independent Sri Lanka. One should not treat this as the entry of a single individual in military garb into politics. Some loquacious politicians in the UNP, who are known for shouting from the mouth, speak various things to justify the selection of Fonseka as the common candidate. Fonseka, in my view, is getting ready to become a military dictator with the creation of a military dictatorship. Please remember what Hitler did to the Weimar Constitution of Germany. ( ) (The Deputy Speaker)

Hon. Minister, please wind up. . . ( () . . ) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala)

Please remember what Pinochet did to Chile in South America. ( ) (The Deputy Speaker)

Hon. Minister, your time is over. . . ( () . . ) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala)

Sir, will you please give me five more minutes? ( ) (The Deputy Speaker)

I am sorry, I cannot. . . ( () . . ) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala)

But, I was told that I will be given five more minutes. ( ) (The Deputy Speaker)

Can you wind up in two more minutes?

. . ( () . . ) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala)

With the agreement of the House, will you give me five more minutes?

( ) (The Deputy Speaker)

Okay. . . ( () . . ) (The Hon. (Prof.) W.A. Wiswa Warnapala)

Who is promoting Fonseka, who before the war, was totally an unknown entity in this country? He was only a soldier with an attractive military garb. I can compare him with one of those strutting soldiers of Adolf Hitler. He needs to be compared with one of those strutting soldiers with those high boots, who has been jumping up and down during the Hitlers regime, who, as the history of the Holocaust mentions, killed millions of Jews in the world. The UNP Front is not a political party. How can you describe it as a political party, though it calls itself a front? It consists of some people who do not possess much of a base in the country. It is experiencing a period of steep political decline in this country. Its support base has eroded largely due to its failure to attract support from its traditional rural base. Its Leader, I refer to the Hon. Ranil Wickremasinghe, indulges only in cheep rhetoric; he is only capable of cheep rhetoric, both inside Parliament and outside. He cannot come to terms with the political culture of the country. With all these faults, the UNP, from its inception in 1946, was a democratic party which stood for some kind of democracy of the conservative creed in this country. That party has now deteriorated into a mere collection of individuals. It, after nearly 65 years of its existence, has failed to produce a candidate to contest the forthcoming Presidential Election. What a tragedy for a grand old Party, the UNP! It, as a Party, cannot go alone because its support base has been shattered and eroded. It now seeks to form a front of parties and this front too is a motley collection. It is a motley collection; it, in political terms, is a bundle of contradictions. There are so many contradictory elements within the Front. There is not a single party with a substantial voter base in the country and those parties who champion the cause of the common candidate are name boards associated with individuals. In my view, a common candidate can be forwarded by an Opposition which has a strong base in the country. But, this Opposition is very much divided, very fragile and fluid and they hold divergent views on politics. A divided Opposition, Mr. Deputy Speaker, cannot launch a strong campaign except to indulge in political slander. Before I come to the other partner of the Front, the JVP, I would like to analyze some of the political slogans of the UNP. Firstly, they want to restore democracy. Let

[ . . ]

2009 08 1625 1626

me first examine this. According to them, democracy has been destroyed. In that contest, one has to ask what they mean by democracy. In a democratic State, the State is a means and only a means to the wellbeing of the individual. The purpose of the State is to do things for the benefit of the individual. He has to realize his best personality within the context of the modern State. The purpose of the democratic State is to administer the community in such a way so as to serve the purposes of its citizens. This is the difference between democracy and authoritarianism. Plato, in his " The Republic" stated that the best and wisest makes the laws, and the rest find their greatest good and happiness in living according to the laws of the land. How, then, are the best and the wisest selected, Mr. Deputy Speaker? Plato, therefore, advocated that these men, his Philosopher Kings, should be entrusted with the government of the State. What I am trying to say, Mr. Deputy Speaker, is that Sarath Fonseka is not a wise man, he is not a man who can become a Philosopher King in this country. Mr. Deputy Speaker, with your permission, let me finally quote from Machiavellis "The Prince" to prove that Sarath Fonskeka is going to fail miserably in this country. Everybody knows Machiavelli's "The Prince". This is what Niccolo Machiavelli says in his "The Prince":

A man can be successful in one situation then fail miserably in another; a policy works well in one moment is a disaster the next. This applies very well to Sarath Fonseka. Thank you, Mr. Deputy Speaker.

UKUWELA PRADESHIYA SABHA AREA: ROADS 0425/09 6. ( ) (The Hon. Ranjith Aluvihare) - (2) : () (i) ; (ii) ; (iii) 2006 ; (iv) 2006 2008 ; (v) ; (vi) ; (vii) , ? () , ? , : () (i) , (ii) , (iii) 2006 , (iv) 2006 2008 , (v) , (vi) , (vii) ? () , ? asked the Minister of Local Government and Provincial Councils: (a) Will he inform this House (i) the types of roads in the Ukuwela Pradeshiya Sabha area; (ii) the name and the length of each road; (iii) the length of each of the aforesaid roads that had been tarred or laid with concrete at the time this Pradeshiya Sabha was elected in the year 2006;

(iv) the names of the roads that have been repaired by laying concrete up to December, 2008, after this Pradeshiya Sabha was elected in the year 2006; (v) the length of each road; (vi) the amount of money spent for it; and (vii) the expenditure head from which this money was spent? (b) If not, why?

(a) Yes,

asked the Minister of Irrigation and Water Management and Ports and Aviation:

(a) Will he inform this House the total number of tanks in the Dambulla Divisional Secretarys Divi-sion in the Matale District, that belong to the Ma-haweli Authority and the Department of Irrigation?

(b) Will he state

(i) separately, the extent of land on the reservations of the aforesaid tanks;

(ii) the year in which surveying was done, last, to identify these reservations;

(iii) whether there are settlers on thon these reserva-tions;

(iv) if so, the legal basis on which they live on those lands; and

(v) if so, that basis and the duration?

(c) If not, why?

Subscriptions : The annual subscription for Official Report of Hansard is Rs. 2,178. A single copy of Hansard is available for Rs. 18.15. (Postage Rs. 2.50) Copies can be obtained by remitting in advance an annual subscription fee to the SUPERINTENDENT, GOVERNMENT PUBLICATIONS BUREAU, No. 132, Maya Avenue, Kirulapone, Colombo 5. The fee should reach him on or before November 30 each year . Late applications for subscriptions will not be accepted.
